REPORT OF BOARD OF PUBLIC WORKS  

In Accidents, Pensions and Vacations more money should
be appropriated to cover the increase in the number of men
on pension and for additional vacations caused by the new
State law which allows man vacation after he has worked
thirty-two weeks in any one year.

In the Alley Department additional money should be
appropriated to cover the increased amount of territory and
in order to maintain the present scehdule of this department.
Attention is also called to the fact of shortage of dumping
grounds. There has been no addition to the culvert in the
Bh Street Dingle this year, consequently this dumping
ground is being used up very quickly.

In the City Property Department the School Board
requests various changes which mean an expenditure of a
large amount of money for alterations and repairs to the
several buildings.

The Forestry Department needs additional money on account of the State Department requiring the suppression
of the gypsy moth, which has not as yet hit Holyoke very
hard blow, although surrounding cities are having great
deal of trouble with the same.

Owing to the increased cost of coal at the present time,
your attention is called to the fact that the appropriation in
this account must be increased.

In Highway repairs will have to be made on all streets
not of permanent construction. Your attention is also called
to the increased number of paved streets that have to be patrolled in order to keep them in clean and sanitary condi- tion. The appropriation in this department must necessarily be increased.

If the present rate of home building is maintained in
the city more money should be appropriated in the sewer accounts, as the building of new housese means the installation
of both main sewers and new connections. This year fifty
per cent  more connections were installed than in  .

  REPORT OF BOARD OF PUBLIC WORKS
During the past year the Board purchased new tractor
combination flusher and truck, new touring car, and snowplow
attachments for trucks.
Your attention is called to the increase in the rental
charge for fire hydrants. This charge was originally Eight
Dollars ($ each and has been increased to Sixteen Dollars ($ ). This will necessitate increasing the appropriation for water rental.
The Board also recommends the purchase of steam roller with steam scarifier attachment, new concrete mixer of
the same capacity as one now in use by the Department. The |
rollers at the Yard at the present time are at least seventeen
( years old, and the concrete mixer has been in continuous
use since  Practically all machines are in worn condition and should be replaced in order to carry on efficiently
the work of the Department.
The Board desires to thank the Mayor and all other City
Officials for their co-operation in carrying on the work of this
Department. |
Annexed you will find detailed accounts of the expenditures in the various departments.
Respectfully submitted,
BOARD OF PUBLIC WORKS, |
J. A. SCHEIBEL, Chairman,
. F. M. O’NEIU,
F. A. MONAT
December .
Attest: G. F. STONE, Asst. Clerk. |

REPORT OF BOARD OF PUBLIC WORKS  
THE BOARD OF PUBLIC WORKS
Established January by His Honor, the Mayor
under the provisions of Title Six, Chapter Thirty-four of an
Act to revise the Charter of the City of Holyoke, which provides for appointment of members by the Mayor without confirmation.

REPORT OF THE 
Child Welfare Commission
Dec.  to Dee. .
To THE HONORABLE, THE MAYOR AND THE BOARD OF ALDERMEN

OF THE City or HoLyoKE, MASSACHUSETTS.

GENTLEMEN: The Child Welfare Commission respectfully submits the following report for the year ending November .

The child hygiene problem today is distinctly different problem than it was when the city of Holyoke first endorsed and financed the small beginnings of local Infant
Hygiene Association.

It was then warning alarm just stirring the mind, heart
and consciousness of nation; today it stands out as problem solved by experience and proven by statistics. Maternal
education, coupled with active pre-natal, maternal and infant
welfare service, if thoroughly and intelligently applied, can
and does reduce maternal and infant mortality.

The earlier efforts of this organization were devoted
entirely to infant welfare work which proved effective as
shown by the following statistics. In Holyoke lost |
  infants (not including out-of-town infants born at
Brightside) out of every births. In  and in
  babies died out of every born.

As even an approximately correct statistical report cannot be made until all of the city’s vital statistics are in and
tabulated, it has seemed best to make no attempt, at this date,
to work out any comparative figures, as has been done in
former years.

  REPORT OF CHILD WELFARE COMMISSION

That the stricter enforcement of the birth registration
laws, as applied to physicians would greatly facilitate the
Jabors of the commission, is obvious; while its necessity from
the point of view of safeguarding the interests of the parent
and child has received national and state publicity without
any very appreciable result, as far as our own and many
other city records show. It should not be possible for a
child’s death to be recorded before its birth, but such has
been known to be the case.

The activities conform closely to those of previous years:
—that is, prenatal care, infant care and the pre-school and
nutrition clinics. |

Under prenatal care we furnish instruction to expectant
mothers in personal hygiene and nourishment. The prenatal
nurse takes blood pressures and makes urinalyses and
reports to physicians. Mothers are placed under physician’s
care and aided in every way in preparation for the event,
When necessary. Ilome conditions are studied and improved ,
as being a.necessary factor condueive to safe and normal
delivery. American customs are taught to the foreign
mothers in the eare of themselves, their homes and  their
elildren. 
The direct infant welfare work consists of furnishing
modified and whole milk of high grade to babies, with special
formule for sick and malnutrition eases. Visits to the

homes by trained nurse for supervision of the care of babies
and the teaching of mothers. “Weekly clinies are held and to
these the mothers may bring their babies to be weighed and
examined by physicians and the mothers themselves advised
or encouraged. Sick babies are always referred back to the
family physician, if there is one, or to one of the parent’s
own choice. If it is city case it is referred to the city phy‘sician and if case of neglect or poverty, care is found
through the station nurses, physicians or hospitals.

A
REPORT OF CHILD WELFARE COMMISSION.  

In the pre-school and nutrition clinics, weighing and
examination of children beyond the baby clinic age is the first
step. Advice is given to mothers by physicians and nurses
and proper care and treatment are found for the most neglected and needy cases. This work is done through fund,
known as the Children’s Health Fund which is raised by
interested workers who know at first hand the conditions in
the case. ,

The prenatal field, while having been developed within
the past three years, after period of ten years of infant
hygiene work, should receive our-first consideration. The
infant mortality rate for Holyoke in this first ten years had
been reduced as far as practicable through the sole agency of.
teaching mothers and the furnishing of prover food and care
to babies. It became apparent here, as in the country at
large, that the mother, her health and environment must be
our next eare. special prenatal nurse has been employed
by the department since April,  During the vear from December  to December  ,
  the prenatal nurse cared for mothers as compared
with mothers for the same period in  Of these,
  were omitted or discharged. |
  cases had from week to weeks care (or less than  

months)—-  still-born, premature.

  eases had months’ care-——  still-born.
  cases had months’ ecare—  still- born, premature.
  cases had months’ care—  maternal death, premature,

  still-born.

  eases had months’ care—no deaths.
  cases had minths’ eare—no deaths.
  cases had months’ eare—no deaths.

The importance of prenata{ care  obvious when these
figures are studied. They show increasing fatalities with
the shorter duration of prenatal supervision of mothers..

o
  REPORT OF CHILD WELFARE COMMISSION

It has also demonstrated that prenatal care is increasing
the number of breast-fed babies, which is an important factor
in baby saving. Of the births, mothers nursed their
babies; nursed from one week to three and one half
months; never nursed due to mothers being obliged to go
to work.

Infant losses, still born, prematures, no miscarriages.

The pressing problem connected with this branch of the
work at this particular time has to do with the ssity of
automobile service for the prenatal nurse. The amount of
work reported above, especially when considering the number
of calls made and what they involve, is remarkable. They
cannot be compared with the calls made by the infant welfare nurse. One call, made on one mother, may require a
half day given to her case. The nurse spends some time
gaining the woman’s confidence. If she speaks no English
the nurse may have to go to the husband at his work, possibly bring him to the home, then may have to go to the City
Hall to Relief Department or City Physician, then back to
the home. Or it may be physician who is turning over
to her needy and neglected case of desertion or illegitimacy
that requires the greatest tact and wisdom, and at the same
time must be handled with expediency. Such case means
numberless trips; some of them, often times as far off as the
City Farm, the hospitals or even out-of-town hospitals and
relief departments. :

The work accomplished would easily have taken the time
of two nurses, large amount of car fare and some taxi fares
at great waste of time and strength, had not Mrs. Ella Perkins, the present prenatal nurse, come into our work owning
her own car which she immediately put at our services, the
city paying the bills for monthly maintenance.

Mrs. Perkins paid  for her machine second-hand, .
  months before she took her present position. It was used
very moderately during that time. Naturally, her work now
requires her to keep her car in constant use. In the years
and months that it has been used for the city it has become
much depreciated in value and now would bring her only

  REPORT OF CHILD WELFARE COMMISSION

$  in trade, or  in forced sale. The cost
of maintaining the car has been increasing the past year.
Something must be done to reimburse Mrs. Perkins and also
settle on the best and yet most reasonal economical means of
providing her with an automobile, if she is expected to
continue to serve the city in this very important branch of
its health work, efficiently and economically.

We respectfully ask Your Honor and Honorable Board of
Aldermen to give this matter your earnest consideration, and
at as early date as feasible, find some means by which it can
be satisfactorily adjusted without hampering the amount or
the efficiency of the work being done.

Records of the infant welfare work for the year show
results as follows:

The daily feeding of these babies means the devoted and
consciencious service by each employee at the milk station.
To them we owe our appreciation.

A station nurse and four assistants are employed in
carrying on this work which must go on Sundays as well as
holidays, and never fail for any cause to send out its daily
feedings to from to babies, according to the season
of the year. )

Eight sub-stations are required with the central station

to handle the milk that its benefits may be carried to every
section of the city. The proprietors of the stores giving the

sub-station privilege deserve the highest commendation for

their generosity and courtesy in handling this branch of our

work. The sub-stations are:—Sta.  Hebert’s Drug Store,

) Ely Street; Sta.  Kilker News Room, Hampden

REPORT OF CHILD WELFARE COMMISSION  
Street; No.  Churchill News Room, High Street; Sta.
 Martin’s Drug Store, Hampden Street; Sta.  Schmitter’s Elmwood Pharmacy, South Street; Sta.  Brosseau’s Oakdale Pharmacy, Sargeant Street; Sta.  Geissler’s Grocery, Vernon Street; Sta.  Ducharme Grocery,
  Appleton Street.

The number of deaths recorded for the year is the highest
in the history of the work. Pneumonia, which during the past
vear has reached almost the epidemic stage, claiming of
the number.

| The milk used for the city’s babies comes from the Lamb
and the Smith dairies in South Hadley. These dairies are
inspected and supervised every month through the cooperation
of the Dairy Department of the Ma achusetts Agricultural
College. Their agent visits the dairies, the local dealers,
and the station at least once month for inspection and
to secure samples of milk for analysis. Reports are received regularly after these visits by the dairyyman, dealer and
commission, giving bacterial content, composition and temperatures; also suggestions and criticisms. This work is done
for Holyoke’s children interestedly and faithfully at the
nominal charge of car fares and materials, or about  per
month. It is of inestimable service to the commission to
know that this, the most vital point in child welfare work, the
milk supply, is receiving this expert supervision.

In the pre-school and nutrition clinic new cases have
been admitted. cases were on at the beginning of the
year and many of these continue under supervision.  
of these children have received hospital care under the Children’s Health Fund previously mentioned. One malnutrition case had  week for six weeks from the same source
for nourishing food.

Three tonsil cases paid their hospital bill but had the
staff physician.

One case for the X-ray, paid Dr. Farr.

Of these were operated on and two were referred to the
Orthopedie Clinic.

Dr. A. L. Kinne is the volunteer physician in charge of
this chinie and Dr. O. T. Fleury has rendered helpful and
interested service during the year. .

The courtesy of the Board of Health in granting the.
commission the use of its rooms for monthly meetings is much
appreciated.

With our present handicaps we cannot hope to plan anything very definite in extension work. few initial steps,
however, could well be taken in certain directions which
would tend to keep us abreast of the forward movement in
child hygiene work.

We plan to open clinic for the prenatal nurse. This
becomes imperative since the growth of her work makes it a
physical impossibility to see all the mothers as frequently as
she should. One afternoon week those mothers who are
able to attend eclinie could be met individually at the station, for counsel and help.

  REPORT OF CHILD WELFARE COMMISSION

We recommend conference of the school medical inspectors and school nurses with the Child Welfare Commission for the purpose of securing cooperation in the attempt

to have every child enter school with as nearly clean bill
of health as possible.

If, as has been stated by educators, one tenth of the public money devoted to the education of children in the schools
of the country is wasted because certain number are not in
a state of health to assimilate the knowledge so freely handed
out to them, is it not plain then, that the best means of conserving school funds in this direction is to start by promoting
the health of the pre-school child?

It would be practical to find cooperating dentists who
would be willing to set aside certain amount of time each
week for the examination of children’s teeth, in their own
offices. Where the parents are unable to pay for care, means
should be found by which the children can get the necessary
attention. Too often malnutrition is due to disinelination
to eat because of the condition of the teeth, and on the train
of this may follow the gravest disorders.

If in the nature of extension work we could only accomplish something during the coming vear in these three directions we would feel we are progressing.

The prenatal and the pre-school work have both demonstrated what, given vision, the gradual initiation of these
extensions of our work can mean to our city.

The need of new building in which to house and carry
on this fundamental health activity, still confronts us. We
are still optimistic knowing that when mother at the station said, ‘‘Holyoke couldn’t do without the milk station
now,’’ she voiced the feeling of thousands of our citizens.

REPORT OF CHILD WELFARE COMMISSION  

The chairman went as delegate to the Thirteenth Annual Convention of the American Child Hygiene Association
at Washington in October. It was notable event, with
Mr. Herbert Hoover im the chair at the opening of the conference.

- Holyoke’s child welfare work is becoming widely known,
and this city is recognized as pioneer among the smaller
cities doing this type of work on municipal basis.

It is with something of pride that we report from Dr.
Merrill E. Champion, of the Massachusetts State Board of
Health, that Holyoke has the lowest mortality of infants under one month of age of any of the largest cities in the
state. He attributes this to the intensive pre-natal and infant welfare work being done in our city.

: There can be no higher ecivie responsibility than this,
assuring the birthright of health to new and we hope better
citizenship of the future.

Respectfully submitted,
LAURA C. WHITTEN, EDWARD P. BAGG, JR., M. D.
FRED H. ALLEN, M. D.
EMILY R. WILSON
JAMES B. BIGELOW, M. D.
MINNIE R. DWIGHT.

Child Welfare Commission.

  REPORT OF CHILD WELFARE COMMISSION
REPORT OF THE MEDICAL DIRECTOR FOR THE
YEAR  .

Mortality statistics are often unreliable and misleading.
Their value depends upon proper interpretation of the facts
presented. It is with some hesitation, therefore, that the
following statistics are presented.

Total birth in Holyoke Jan.  to Dec. ,....... )
Total births in Holyoke of infants whose parents live
outside of the City,  ... cc     )
| )
Total deaths of infants under one vear of age,...... )
Total deaths of infants under one year of age whose

residence is outside the City... ..  ...  ... cc     )

  )
Mortality rate using and as basis of comPULALTION Loe ce   e ete ewe   tenes per  
Mortality rate using and as basis of comPULATION Lo. cer          re ec sees  per  

The difference between these is marked. When babies
Whose residenee is given as Holvoke die in other cities of
Massachustts or even in other of the New England states than
Massachusetts, these deaths are registered in the Holyoke
death statistics. It seems only fair, then, to exclude from
Hlolyoke statistics, deaths occurring here of babies whose residence is outside the city. Towever, for the sake of comparison, all cities should follow the same procedure an! data on
this point is not given in statisties with which we are familiar.

Another important fact to note is the time of the infant's
death. Of the deaths in  or occurred within hours after birth, obviously meaning, in many cases,
faulty prenatal conditions or trouble at the time of birth.
Twelve, or died between the first and seventh days,
making total of or who did not live long enough
to be appreciably influenced by postnatal care. There were
  still births, and classed as premature at birth.—less

. .

. REPORT OF CHILD WELFARE COMMISSION  

than in but more than in or  when still
births were recorded for each year, while only si premature
infants in and in died in infancy.

These figures are disappointing in view of the fact that
our prenatal work is well established. Yet here again the
figures may be very misleading, for it is not at all improbable
that women having had miscarriages previously, were, with
greater watchfulness given during the prenatal periud, able
to go to full term or have premature babies. The data how.
ever are not available as yet in sufficient numbers of cases to

- make any conclusions justifiable.

Attention should also be given to the comparative rate
of babies having oversight of the commission and those not ,
having such. During the year there were deaths
of children under one year, who were classed as having supervision of the Commission. With total of cases this
makes mortality rate of per as compared with rate
of for the city as whole, whereas the mortality rate for
the babies not under the supervision of the Commissicn is
  per  However this comparison may not be just
one, due to the inclusion in the babies classed under our
supervision, those who remained only short time in this class,
and who either did not do well or became dissatisfied and
sought advice elsewhere. .

them and to Prof. Yaxis in particular the commission is much
indebted.

These counts are taken from samples of formule put up
in bottles ready to send out to the babies, and show the care
taken in handling throughout the entire process of their preparation, from the farm, through the various stages of transportation, bottling and the mixing of the formule. With
more adequate quarters and better cooling facilities which we
, hope to have in another year, these figures should be materially reduced. Constant watchfulness and the maintenance at all times of hygienic rules for handling the milk are
absolutely essential.
Respectfully submitted,
FRED H. ALLEN, M.D. 
Medical Director.

REPORT OF THE
Fire Comnnissioners
To THE HoNoRABLE Mayor AND BOARD OF ALDERMEN:

GENTLEMEN :—We take pleasure in submitting to you in
accordance with the City Ordinance, the report of the activities of the Holyoke Fire Department for the year ending
November .

The Board of Fire Commissioners, consisting of Arthur
K. French, David Clark and Joseph C. Doyle, met January
Sth, and organized by electing Arthur E. French as
Chairman, and David Clark, Vice-Chairman. Commissioner

Clark was removed from the Board on January  th and
George H. Lane was appointed to fill the vacancy.

There have been fires this year. The losses on
buildings amounted to and on contents, making total fire loss of The property endangered by fire was valued at and
the insurance on said property amounted to .
Insurance companies paid the sum of leaving a
net uninsured loss of an average of  fire.
The total loss per capita was and the uninsured loss,
$.  per capita.

The largest fires during the year were as follows:
Robert C. Hunter building, North East Street, 
Collins Murray, furniture store, ............  
Ducharme Poitras, city stables, ............  
Buildings from to Park Street, ........  
Fitzsimmons Block, Main Street,..........  
Y. M. GC. AL we             

  REPORT OF FIRE COMMISSIONERS

The most disastrous of these fires occurred on the morning of May  th. The department was called to fire at
the City Stables on Ely Street at A. M. Owing to the
size of the fire and the number of horses in the stable, a
general alarm was sounded, which brought all members of
both platoons to the fire. At A. M., while engaged at
the Ely Street fire, at its height, fire broke out on Park
Street which spread from to  and which caused a
heavy loss. Twelve horses were burned to death at the
Ely Street fire. The cause of these fires has not been determined.

We regret to report that Veronica Yalga, four years
of age, of Walnut Street, died on January  as the
result of burns. The Department was not called for fire
in this instance.

Fire Prevention Week, October  nd to  th,  was
observed extensively by the Department by order of the
Mayor and Board of Fire Commissioners. thorough eampaign of publicity was outlined so that the importance of

| Fire Prevention might be realized by everyone. The Chamber of Commerce offered three five dollar gold pieces as prizes
to the school children who would submit the best essays on
Fire Prevention. The large number of scholars who ecompeted testifies to the amount of interest taken by the city
at large. parade of all the fire apparatus was staged during the week; write-ups were prepared for the press each |
day, and slides were used in all the theatres in the city.

As compensation for the great amount of effort expended, our fire losses for October were surprisingly small,
the actual loss being  as against over  for
the other eleven months of the year. The pubriec is to be
highly commended for its spirit of eo-operation with the
Department in helping to keep down the fire losses. In
this connection we wish to thank the local theatres, the press
and all others who assisted in this work.

REPORT OF FIRE COMMISSIONERS  
Two firemen were retired on pension: Albert Tardy of
Pump No. was retired on March  st,  he being over
sixty vears of age, and having been in the Department
thirty one years. Patrick J. Kennedy of Pump No. was also
retired on pension due to ill health, he having served in the
Department over twenty three years. He was retired on
November  th,  William J. Russell of Main Street
Was appointed permanent member of the Department.

For several years, the Fire Commissioners and Chief
Ilurley have recommended the complete motorization of the
Department, and we are pleased to report that their recommendations have been carried out. new city service ladder truck was purchased from the American LaFrance Fire
Engine Company for  which takes the place of the two
horse drawn pieces of apparatus which were stationed at Elmwood and the Highlands. This apparatus has large territory to cover, taking in from Smiths Ferry on the north
to the West Springfield line on the south, and all of West
Holyoke. After due consideration, it was decided to instal
this piece at the Highland fire station. This necessitated
some changes in the Highland and Elmwood companies, which
left company of six men on each shift at the Elmwood station and two companies of five men each at the Highland
station. We believe that the efficiency of the Department
is greatly increased by the purchase of this piece of apparatus,
as it means the abolition of two practically useless horsedrawn truck companies, and the installation of first-class —
truck company, which, although somewhat removed from
Elmwood, provides much greater protection for the people
of that district than did the horse-drawn apparatus.

In this connection, we would again call vour attention
to the necessity of fire station midway between Elmwood
and the Highlands. This district is growing very rapidly,
and with but one ladder truck for Elmwood and the Ilighlands, great deal more could be accomplished with one .

  REPORT OF FIRE COMMISSIONERS

station containing enough apparatus to cover the territory.
Fire Departments through the country are making an effort to
centralize their stations as much as possible, this being made
possible through the increased speed of the motor apparatus
over the horse-drawn apparatus. Figures received from the
Board of Public Works show that the saving in fuel, lighting, ete., together with the amount received through the sale
of the vast properties at the Highlands and Elmwood, would
in few years, pay for the cost of the new building.

Mr. Walter Seott of New York City honored the City
by presenting to the Fire Department six per cent
bond to create fund from which gold medal is to be
awarded annually to that member of the Holyoke Fire Department, whose acts of valor during the year were the most
meritorious. Board of Award was established, consisting of the Board of Fire Commissioners, the Chief and the
Deputy Chiefs, who shall meet annually in November to
decide who, in their opinion, is entitled to receive the medal.
The year for awarding the medal is to extend from November Ist  Oetober  st inclusive. The Board of Award unanimously decided to award the medal this year to Captain
Walter Scott Watt or Truck Company No.  who saved from a
smoke-filled building at Lyman Street, sick woman, who
otherwise would probably have suffocated. This act occurred
on March  th,  .

We are pleased to state that the records show splendid

: spirit of cooperation on the part of the firemen in responding
to seeond and general alarms. We had three second alarms
and one general alarm during the year, and the response in all
cases Is splendid endorsement of the two-platoon system.
We have installed system with the aid of the Telephone
Company, by which the fire alarm operator at Headquarters
notifies the Telephone Exchange that there is second or
general alarm, and informs them which platoon is off duty.

. as the Telephone Exchange has been supplied with cards,

REPORT OF FIRE COMMISSIONERS  
giving names, addresses, and telephone numbers through
which all members of the platoons may be reached, the operator, upon notification, then calls all members of the platoon off duty. The Department feels deeply grateful to the
Supervisor and members of the Telephone Exchange who
have so kindly assisted in this work.

We respectfully recommend the following for your consideration: ;

( Our first and most important recommendation is
that new fire station be built midway between the Highlands and Elmwood, near the corner of Northampton and
Sargeant Streets, and that the stations and lots in those districts be sold. We recommend that this be done at an early
date, as the condition of the Highland station will necessitate
the making of repairs throughout the building. The roof
sags, allowing the rain to leak through; the apparatus floor
should be laid in concrete to conform with the law in that
respect, and the back of that station, which was used to
stable the horses should be remodeled.

( We recommend the purchase of an automobile for
the use of the Deputy Chiefs. This is to replace the car now
in use, which was purchased in May,  .

( We advise the purchase of  -gallon pump for

. the South Holyoke Station, to replace one of the old Knox
ears there. These Knox cars have been in the Department
nearly thirten years, and as they are no longer manufactured, |
it is very difficult to replace the parts as they become worn.
The City of Holyoke is rated in the third class vy the New
England Insurance Exchange, and we are informed by its engineer that by making certain improvements in our Department, we will be placed in the second class, distinction enjoyed by but few cities in the State. One weakness, according to the engineer, is that we have not the required
pumping capacity.

  REPORT OF FIRE COMMISSIONERS

; We recommend that the floor at the South Holyoke Station be laid in concrete. There are three pieces of
motor apparatus in this Station and we feel that the floor
needs attention this year.

REPORT OF FIRE COMMISSIONERS  
ee
We regret to report that we have lost two men by death
during the last year, viz:
Captain James J. Long of Pumping Company No.  .
Capt. Long was appointed to the call force on September
 th,  and appointed call Lieutenant on February  th,
 On December  th, he was appointed to the
permanent force and January  d, his rank was increased to that of Captain. Captain Long was overcome
at fire at the Parsons Paper Company, and although complaining of illness, he remained on duty. About four days
later, August  th,  he died suddenly while working at
the Central Fire Station. :
Fireman Edward M. Clancy, of Truck Company No.  ,
who was appointed February  th,  died December  th,
 His record was above reproach and his death was a
 distinet loss to the Department. |

year:

HOSE
In conformity with the standard set by the National
Loard of Fire Underwriters, we are testing our hose each
spring and fall at and pounds pressure, respectively.
Owing to the shortage of funds this year, we were unable to
purchase anv new hose. We have condemned feet of
hose during the last two vears, which should be replaced this
year. .

CONCLUSION
We desire to express to the Honorable Mayor, the Board
of Aldermen, the Board of Public Works, the Board of Water
Commissioners, the Gas and Electric Department, the City
Clerk, the City Treasurer, the City Auditor, the City Marshal
and the police officers, to the Superintendent of Schools, the
Superintendent of Parks, and other City Officials, our sinfe re appreciation of the many acts of courtesy shown us durIng the past year, and especially to the Holyoke Street Railway in behalf of the members of the Department, for the
privilege of riding on the company’s ears when on duty without expense, and for their general cooperation with the Department. .
Respectfully yours,
ARTHUR E. FRENCH,
JOSEPH C. DOYLE
GEORGE Hl. LANE,,
Board of Fire Commissioners.

: REPORT OF THE
To the Honorable the Mayor and Board of Aldermen

GENTLEMEN :—I herewith present the annual statement
of the receipts and expenditures for the fiscal year  in
the form and manner required by the Commonwealth.

The accounts of the City Clerk, Milk Inspector, Water,
and Gas and Electric departments have been audited and
found correct; the receipts properly recorded and promptly
deposited, and the expenditures approved in due form.

) The Tax Collector’s books and entries have been audited ,
as far as possible. The postings here number thousands, and
as each must be separately checked, it takes months to complete the work.

This report also contains detailed report of the expenditures in the Contingent account, City Indebtedness, Tax
Collector’s Exhibit, bonds issued during the year with the
purpose for which they were issued, the cash on hand, borrowing capacity and comparative debt statement for the
past years.

Bonds amounting to  were issued this year for
the following named purposes: Highways, Sewers,
$ Sidewalks, Schools, Playgrounds,
$ .

é
  REPORT OF CITY AUDITOR

Payment on the debt, including additions to the Sinking
Fund amounted to  as follows: City Debt, ;
Gas and Electric Debt, Holyoke and Westfield R.
It., Water, .

The total net debt all sources is decrease of
$  over last year. This does not include the Temporary
Loans which are the same as last year.

The borrowing capacity is an increase of ,-  over  .
Respectfully submitted,
DANIEL W. KENNEY,
City Auditor.

THE WHITING STREET FUND ,
This is Fund for the relief of worthy poor who are
not receiving aid from the City. It originated in the will
of Whiting Street of Northampton, probated in that city .
Sept. bequeathing to sundry cities and towns in this
vieinity  for the purpose before mentioned; and cer tain other sums for the support of certain relatives. Of
the total amount, Holyoke’s share was Under the
care of the executors, the original bequest increased in value
and after the death of the last legatee the executors requested the Supreme Judicial Court to determine how the increment should be disbursed. On July  the Court decided that the increment should follow the original intent of
the donor, and Holyoke’s share, under the decision, became
$  for the Trust, and an additional  for income, being the earnings since the last income award was
made the city in  .
Total Trust Fund ....................$ 

 REPORT OF CITY AUDITOR
THE WALTER SCOTT FUND

This trust was created March  under deed of
gift from Col. Walter Scott of New York to create in perpetuity, trust, the prods of which are to be used to purchase
annually two gold medals. one of which is to be presented to
such member of the Fire Department of the City of Holyoke
as, in the opinion of the Board of Fire Commissioners, has
distinguished himself for valor in the performance of his
duty; the other to be presented to such member of the Police
Department of the City of Holyoke as, in the opinion of the
City Marshal has distinguished himself for valor in the performance of his duty.

REPORT OF CITY ENGINEER  

During the past year this department furnished plans,

specifications, lines, grades and estimates for the bridges,
pavements, sewers, sidewalks, etc., constructed.

Estimates were also furnished for loans for other public
improvements.

In preparing the budget for Mayor Cronin sought
advice from many of the heavy taxpayers of the City as to
municipal improvements for the year demanded by the various departments. At meeting held in the Nonotuck Hotel
subcommittees were appointed to investigate and report on
the different projects. At the request of the Mayor the
City Enginer attended metings of the several committees. He
also accompanied these committees on their tours of inspection and prepared for their use estimates and reports on
bridges, pavements, schools and other public buildings.

BRIDGES

Following is lst of the new bridges completed and
opened to traffic during the year  .

Appleton Street over the  nd level canal
Bridge Street over the  nd level canal
Jackson Street over the  nd level canal
Lyman Street over the  nd level canal
Lyman Street over the Ist level canal

The general design of the bridge over the first level canal
on Appleton Street built in was followed in the later
canal bridges, thus giving the City six new structures appropriate to the locations and safe for modern traffic.

Concrete was used in all the bridges for the protection of
the steel and as floor slab on account of its strength and
permanency.

  REPORT OF CITY ENGINEER

The contracts for three new bridges were awarded so late

in the year that it was impossible to complete them

- before winter. Concrete construction is most difficult and
uncertain in cold weather unless special measures are taken
to prevent freezing. If possible municipal improvements
involving the use of this material should begin early and be
completed under favorable weather conditions.

The City Engineer prepared plans and specifications
for new wood block floor for the country bridge over the
Connecticut River to South Hadley Falls. The contract
was awarded bv the Board of Public Works to the Standard
Engineering Company of Toledo, Ohio, as was also the new
wood block floor on the Willimansett bridge. Recommendations were made by the City Engineer for extensive repairs
to the steel work of this bridge.

REPORT OF THE
Board of Health
To The ToNorasLe, THe Mayor Anp Tue BoarD oF ALDERMEN OF TuiE City oF TLOLYOKE:

GENTLEMEN :—The forty-seeond annual statement of all
matters pertaining to Board of Health for the year ending
November thirtieth, nineteen hundred twenty two is hereby
submitted for your consideration.

ORGANIZATION

The members of the Board of Health met for organization the first Monday in February, nineteen hundred twenty
two and elected the following officers:—Peter W. Waters,
Chairman, Dolor  Beaupre, M. D., Secretary.

Appended are the reports of the Health Officer. Inspector
of Plumbing, Sanitary Inspectors, Inspector of Meat and
Provisions, Milk Inspector, Bacteriologist, Dispensary and
Hospitals, also the mortality tables and records of the registration of the contageious diseases with reeord of the office
work and statement of the receipts and expenditures.

Regular weekly meetings of the Board have been held.
Many complaints of all kinds have been received and careful
attention has been given to each one and steps taken to better conditions and remove the causes.

VITAL STATISTICS

During the year eight hundred thirty five deaths occured
in the etiy, giving death rate of per cent per thousand
population. There were non-residents and seventy-one
still births recorded.

REPORT OF THE

Plumbing permits granted ................ |

Plumbing inspections ................-..-.  

Water tests made ............... 

The usual number of complaints have been investigated
and nuisanees abated where found.

A decided increase in plumbing is noted and the department has been taxed at times to give prompt service.

The Inspector would again eall attention to the growing danger from explosions of hot water boilers. With the
installation of many heaters the old serviees In many cases
being practically filled with rust or provided with pressure
regulators and with no provisions or law making the use of
the safety valve compulsory, the danger of explosions is apparent. In many cities the water department provides for
the use of the relief or safety valve and its inspectors enforce
the provisions.

Your Inspector would suggest that mandatory laws be
passed providing for the installations of safety valves on all
vessels, boilers, ete., where water is heated under pressure.

Holvoke, Mass., November .
To the Honorable, the Mayor and Board of Aldermen of the

City of Holyoke:

GENTLEMEN :—In commonplianee with the City Ordinance, have the honor herewith to submit for vour consideration the annual report of the Department of Police for
the vear ending November .

. ORGANIZATION

The regular force consists of Marshal, assistant Marshal, Captain, Lieutenant, five Sergeants, Chief Inspector,
five Inspectors and seventy-five patrolman, four of whom

are detailed in the office, and two in the Deteetive Bureau.

REPORT OF THE

Report of the Sealer of Weights and Measures for the
vear ending November  th,  .

To the Honorable, the Mayor and Board of Aldermen.

GENTLEMEN: have the honor of presenting to you, the
seventeenth annual report of the Weights and Measures Department of the City of Holvoke. for the vear ending November  th.  .

In presenting this report, wish to repeat my recommendation of former vears, that the work of this department
has increased to such proportions, that it is imperative that
the office of Deputy Sealer be created.

T wish to thank the City Officials. the Manufacturers and
the Merchants, for the courteous manner in which this department has been received, in the discharge of its duties.

A detailed report of the work of this department is herewith presented.

Respectfully submitted,
| JOSEPH D. GODDU,
Sealer.

REPORT OF THE
a Veterinary Surgeon
December 
To His Honor the Mayor and Board of Aldermen, Holyoke,
Massachusetts.

GENTLEMEN: herewith submit to you my report, as
inspector of animals, for the year  .

I have made regular inspection of all the dairies and
stables within the city limits, and inspected fifty-two dairies:
Number of dairy cattle .........  ...     

”? ”” SWING Lo.         eens  
- ”? ”? Horses ....      eens  

Also, have inspected four hundred and twenty-five
head of cattle coming in from other states. have examined
and released one hundred and ten horses coming in from
other states. also quaranteened thirty-two dogs which
were bitten by the rabid dogs, and eight which proved to be
affeeted with rabies. Of four of these dogs which were
bitten by the rabid dogs two died with rabies. While in
quarantine, the heads of these animals were sent to the
Department of Animal Industry in Boston, and all were
found to be affected with rabies.

I have tested number of cattle for tuberculosis, and
condemned twenty-four head which were affected with this
disease on Post Mortem.

At present find the city is without any infectious disease among the animals.

Signed,
DR. J. J. MOYNIHAN,
Inspector of Animals.

REPORT OF THE SUPERINTENDENT
HOo.LyokeE City Farm
To the Honorable, the Board of Overseers of the Poor:

GENTLEMEN :—I respectfully present herewith the annual report of the Holyoke City Farm for the fiscal year
ending November .

The total number of persons cared for was  of whom
  were admitted during the year. Of this number  
were admitted as Hospital Patients.

Forty-three sick children were admitted to the ‘‘Children’s Ward’’ in the Hospital Department; all of these have
been discharged as cured except three.

The production from the farm this year exds all past
records; the estimated value of all products is about .

All statistics of general interest will be exhibited by the
following tables: .

RECOMMENDATIONS

We wish to renew our suggestion of last year that a
veranda in connection with the Nursery would be of great
benefit in providing for the care and comfort of the many
children we are taking eare of.

Painting the exterior of the old barns and sheds, also
the exterior of the ‘‘Home Building’’ is necessary and would
add to the appearance as well as preserve the usefulness of
the property.

We wish to thank the Overseers of the Poor, the City
Almoner, the Clerks in his office and the City Physician for
their kind co-operation and courtesy.

REPORT OF OVERSEERS OF THE POOR ool
And we sincerely wish to thank Mayor John F. Cronin
for his unfailing interest and the many kindnesses shown the
people at this institution.
JOHN J. O’CONNOR,
Superintendent of City Farm.

REPORT OF THE
To THE HonoraBLE Mayor or THE City or HOLYOKE:

I submit herewith my report for the year  .

The following are the cases which were settled during the
year in the courts and the amount of settlement in each case:

| Bridget Dowd (personal injuries, defective way)  
Margaret McCarthy (personal injuries, defective

WAY) Loic   cc         eenees  

Abbie Gibson (personal injuries, defective way).. 
| David Maloney (personal injuries, defective way)  
Catherine McCarthy (personal injuries, defective

WAY)  cc             
Massachusetts Baking Company (Damage to property on account of obstruction in sewer)....  
Mary M. Prew (Damage to land caused by alleged

defective construction and maintenance of

highway) ......     t ees  

I have rendered an unusually large number of written
opinions to the different municipal departments.

The work of revising and compiling the ordinances was
commenced some months ago and considerable progress has
been made in the work. number of public hearings were
held and much interest was shown in the matter and many
valuable suggestions received from the various City officials
and departments and other individuals and organizations.
The time for reporting on the work to the Board of Alder- !

. I

REPORT OF CITY SOLICITOR  
men has been extended to February The work of
revising the building ordinances regard as one of great
importance. would suggest that further public hearings
be held in this matter before any proposed changes are reported so that all interested parties may be given the fullest
opportunity to be heard.

The Manager of the Gas Electric Department has
called to my attention certain contracts which are in existence between the Holvoke Water Power Company and other
corporations in the City of Llolyoke in regard to the use for
hghting purposes by these corporations of electrical energy
purehased by them from the Holyoke Water Company. He
also submitted to me ecorrespondenee between himself and
the officials of the Holvoke Water Power Company in regard to these eontracts. After the matter was referred to
me sent communication to the Holyoke Water Power Company to the effect that in my opinion the sale of electrical
energy under these contracts to purchaser, who with the
knowledge of the Holyoke Water Power Company was using
it for lighting purposes, was an attempt by the Holyoke Water
Power Company to exercise legal rights which were outside
the scope of any powers conferred upon it by its charter.
From the tenor of the communications received by myself and
the Manager of the Gas Electrie Department from the
Holyoke Water Power Company, it is clearly apparent that ,
the Holyoke Water Power Company intends to assert rights
in regard to the manufacture, sale and distribution or electricity within the limits of the City of Holyoke, the exercise of
which. will, make them competitors of the Gas Electric

| department in the sale of electricity to be used for hghting
purposes,

The Holyoke Water Power Company in the year  ,
a short tome after it had sold its plants to the City of Hol- yoke, by amendment of its charter was authorize’ to manua
  REPORT OF CITY SOLICITOR
facture electricity in the City of Holyoke ‘‘for power purposes,’’ the authority was further amended by Legislative
Act in  .

After careful study of the circumstances under which
these Legislative Acts were passed, believe that the Massachusetts Legislature did not grant, and did not Intend to
grant, to the Holyoke Water Power Company the rights
which it now claims to have under these Legislative Acts.

I recommend that legal action be taken by tne City of

| Holyoke in the near future to protect the municipal lighting
plant from any attempt at competition from corporation
which, feel, has morally and legally obligated itself to the
citizens of the City of Holyoke, not to engage in such competition.

I wish to thank the various officials of the City for their
kindly assistance and co-operation during my term of office.

. Respectfully submitted,
THOMAS C. MAHER,
City Solicitor.

CITY OF HOLYOKE.
In the: Year One Thousand Nine Hundred and Twenty-two.
AN ORDINANCE
To Provide for the Appointment of Commissioner of
Soldiers’ Relief.
Be it ordained by the Board of Aldermen of the city of

Holyoke, as follows.

Section  The mavor shall as soon after the passage
hereof as is practical and thereafter annually in the month
of January appoint, subject to confirmation by the board of
aldermen, commissioner of soldiers’ relief, who shall, unless
sooner removed, hold his office for term of one vear from
the first Monday in February in the year of his appointment
or until his suecessor shall be appointed and shall enter upon
the performance of his duties. vaeaney in said office
may be filled for the unexpired term at any time in the manner above provided for an original appointment. The incumbent of said office may be removed at the will of the
mayor and aldermen.

Section  Said commissioner shall perform such duties
relative to the disbursement of state aid, military aid and
the furnishing of soldiers’ relief as the committee on state
and military aid and soldiers’ relief of the board of aldermen
may from time to time authorize or direct; and shall perform
the duties of burial agent if and when appointed by the
mayor.  Ife shall also perform such other duties as the board
of aldermen or the committee on state and military aid and
soldiers’ relief of said board may from time to time direct.

Section  The annual compensation of said commissioner for the performance of all duties provided for by this
ordinanee shall be in the sum of three hundred dollars. 

Section  The person appointed by the mayor to see
that every cemetery lot where there is grave of soldier or
sailor is suitably kept and cared for as provided by section
twenty-two of chapter one hundred and fifteen of ‘the General Laws, is hereby designated as the supervisor of soldiers’
and sailors’ graves.

Section oO. This ordinance shall take effect upon its
passage.

Approved February .

CITY ORDINANCES 
CITY OF HOLYOKE.
In the Year One Thousand Nine Hundred and Twenty-Two.
AN ORDINANCE
Relative to Hawkers and Peddlers
Be it Ordained by the Board of Aldermen of the.city of

Holyoke, as follows.

Section  No person shall sell or expose for sale as a
hawker and peddler in this city any fish, fruit or vegetables
unless he is duly licensed therefor by the Board of Aldermen.

Section  The Board of Aldermen may grant license
to any person of good repute for morals and integrity, and
after the applicant has presented certificate from the Sealer

‘ of Weights and Measures stating that all weighing or measuring devices intended to be used by such person have been
duly inspected and sealed as required by law, and upon other
conditions as they may deem expedient, and may revoke the
same at their discretion, and the record of the license as
granted shall be kept by the City Marshal. The use of and .
possession by such person with intent to use any false or unsealed weighing or measuring devices shall be sufficient cause
for the revocation of his license.

Section  Lieenses granted hereunder shall expire one
year from date of issue, unless sooner revoked, and no license
shall be transferable. For every license so granted there
shall be paid to the City Clerk the sum of fifteen dollars for
the use of the city.

Section  Every person licensed to peddle as aforesaid ,
shall be assigned number by the City Marshal; shall be provided by the said Marshal with badge, bearing such number,
of such type and design as may be approved by the said
Marshal, and it shall be conspicuously worn by the person to

ot  CITY ORDINANCES

whom it is issued; shall be provided by the said Marshal with
a number plate of such type and design as is approved by the
said Marshal, the number and date of expiration of such
license shall be attached to each side of every vehicle or receptacle used by the licensee as conveyance of articles offered for sale by him; and, when his license is demanded of
him by any police officer or the Sealer of Weights and Measures, he shall forthwith exhibit it, and, if he neglects or
refuses so to do, he shall be subject to the same penalty as if
he had no license.

Section  Whoever shall offend against or fail to comply with any of the provisions of this ordinance, shall for
each offence, forfeit and pay penalty of not more than
twenty dollars.

Section  All the provisions of this ordinance shall be
incorporated into every license which shall be granted
under it.

Section  An ordinance entitled ‘‘An Ordinance relative to Ilawkers and Peddlers’’ approved May  and

sections five and six of chapter of the revised ordinances
of and any or all ordinances or parts thereof inccnsistent herewith are hereby repealed.

Section  This ordinance shall take effect upon its
passage.

February .
